<p><b>Audi</b> (<small>pronounced</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈʔaʊ̯dɪ ʔaːˈgeː]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Audi_AG.ogg" title="File:Audi AG.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Audi_AG.ogg" class="internal" title="Audi AG.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is a German <a href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile manufacturer">automobile manufacturer</a> that designs, engineers, produces, markets and distributes <a href="/wiki/Luxury_vehicle" title="Luxury vehicle">luxury vehicles</a>. Audi is member of <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> and has its roots at <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt" title="Ingolstadt">Ingolstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, Germany. Audi-branded vehicles are produced in nine production facilities worldwide.</p>
<p>The origins of the company are complex, going back to the early 20th century and the initial enterprises (<a href="/wiki/Horch" title="Horch">Horch</a> and the <i>Audiwerke</i>) founded by engineer <a href="/wiki/August_Horch" title="August Horch">August Horch</a>; and two other manufacturers (<a href="/wiki/DKW" title="DKW">DKW</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wanderer_(car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wanderer (car)">Wanderer</a>), leading to the foundation of <a href="/wiki/Auto_Union" title="Auto Union">Auto Union</a> in 1932. The modern era of Audi essentially began in the 1960s when Auto Union was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> from <a href="/wiki/Daimler-Benz" title="Daimler-Benz">Daimler-Benz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vw-holdings-2009_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vw-holdings-2009-9">[9]</a></sup> After relaunching the Audi brand with the 1965 introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Audi_F103" title="Audi F103">Audi F103</a> series, Volkswagen merged Auto Union with <a href="/wiki/NSU_Motorenwerke" title="NSU Motorenwerke">NSU Motorenwerke</a> in 1969, thus creating the present day form of the company.</p>
<p>The company name is based on the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> translation of the surname of the founder, <a href="/wiki/August_Horch" title="August Horch">August Horch</a>. "Horch", meaning "listen" in <a href="/wiki/German_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="German (language)">German</a>, becomes "audi" in Latin. The four rings of the Audi logo each represent one of four car companies that banded together to create Audi's predecessor company, Auto Union. Audi's slogan is <a href="/wiki/Vorsprung_durch_Technik" class="mw-redirect" title="Vorsprung durch Technik">Vorsprung durch Technik</a>, meaning "Advancement through Technology". However, since 2007 Audi USA has used the slogan "Truth in Engineering".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Audi, along with BMW and Mercedes are among the best-selling luxury automobile brands in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_the_company_and_its_name">Birth of the company and its name</span></h3>
<p>Originally in 1885, <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a> company Wanderer was established, later becoming a branch of Audi AG. Another company, NSU, which also later merged into Audi, was founded during this time, and later supplied the chassis for <a href="/wiki/Gottlieb_Daimler" title="Gottlieb Daimler">Gottlieb Daimler</a>'s four-wheeler.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 November 1899, <a href="/wiki/August_Horch" title="August Horch">August Horch</a> (1868–1951) established the company <b>A. Horch &amp; Cie.</b> in the <a href="/wiki/Ehrenfeld,_Cologne" title="Ehrenfeld, Cologne">Ehrenfeld</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. Three years later in 1902 he moved with his company to <a href="/wiki/Reichenbach_im_Vogtland" title="Reichenbach im Vogtland">Reichenbach im Vogtland</a>. On May, 10th, 1904 he founded the <b>August Horch &amp; Cie. Motorwagenwerke AG</b>, a joint-stock company in <a href="/wiki/Zwickau" title="Zwickau">Zwickau</a> (State of <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a>).</p>
<p>After troubles with Horch chief financial officer, August Horch left Motorwagenwerke and founded in Zwickau on 16 July 1909, his second company, the <b>August Horch Automobilwerke GmbH</b>. His former partners sued him for trademark infringement. The German <a href="/wiki/Reichsgericht" title="Reichsgericht">Reichsgericht</a> (Supreme Court) in Leipzig,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> eventually determined that the Horch brand belonged to his former company.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Typ_E_(1923).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg/220px-Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg/330px-Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg/440px-Audi_Typ_E_%281923%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1417" data-file-height="1063" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Typ_E_(1923).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi Type E</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since August Horch was prohibited from using "Horch" as a trade name in his new car business, he called a meeting with close business friends, Paul and Franz Fikentscher from Zwickau, Germany. At the apartment of Franz Fikentscher, they discussed how to come up with a new name for the company. During this meeting, Franz's son was quietly studying Latin in a corner of the room. Several times he looked like he was on the verge of saying something but would just swallow his words and continue working, until he finally blurted out, "Father&#160;– <i><a href="/wiki/Audi_alteram_partem" title="Audi alteram partem">audiatur et altera pars</a></i>...&#160;wouldn't it be a good idea to call it <i>audi</i> instead of <i>horch</i>?"<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> "Horch!" in German means "Hark!" or "hear", which is "Audi" in the singular imperative form of "audire" – "to listen" – in Latin. The idea was enthusiastically accepted by everyone attending the meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> On 25 April 1910 the <b>Audi Automobilwerke GmbH Zwickau</b> (from 1915 on <b>Audiwerke AG Zwickau</b>) was entered in the company's register of Zwickau registration court.</p>
<p>The first Audi automobile, the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Type_A" title="Audi Type A">Audi Type A</a> 10/22&#160;hp (16&#160;kW) Sport-Phaeton, was produced in the same year,<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle1-17">[17]</a></sup> followed by the successor <a href="/wiki/Audi_Type_B" title="Audi Type B">Type B</a> 10/28PS in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audi started with a 2,612&#160;cc <a href="/wiki/Inline-four_engine" title="Inline-four engine">inline-four engine</a> model Type A, followed by a 3,564&#160;cc model, as well as 4,680&#160;cc and 5,720&#160;cc models. These cars were successful even in sporting events. The first <a href="/wiki/Straight-six_engine" title="Straight-six engine">six-cylinder</a> model Type M, 4,655&#160;cc appeared in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Audi_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Audi-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>August Horch left the <i>Audiwerke</i> in 1920 for a high position at the ministry of transport, but he was still involved with Audi as a member of the board of trustees. In September 1921, Audi became the first German car manufacturer to present a production car, the Audi Type K, with left-handed drive.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle3_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle3-20">[20]</a></sup> Left-hand drive spread and established dominance during the 1920s because it provided a better view of oncoming traffic, making overtaking safer.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle3_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle3-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_merger_of_the_four_companies_under_the_logo_of_four_rings">The merger of the four companies under the logo of four rings</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Auto_Union" title="Auto Union">Auto Union</a></div>
<p>In August 1928, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B8rgen_Skafte_Rasmussen" title="Jørgen Skafte Rasmussen">Jørgen Rasmussen</a>, the owner of <a href="/wiki/Dampf-Kraft-Wagen" class="mw-redirect" title="Dampf-Kraft-Wagen">Dampf-Kraft-Wagen</a> (DKW), acquired the majority of shares in Audiwerke AG.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle4_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle4-21">[21]</a></sup> In the same year, Rasmussen bought the remains of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile manufacturer">automobile manufacturer</a> <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_(car)" title="Rickenbacker (car)">Rickenbacker</a>, including the manufacturing equipment for eight-cylinder engines. These engines were used in <i>Audi Zwickau</i> and <i>Audi Dresden</i> models that were launched in 1929. At the same time, six-cylinder and four-cylinder (<a href="/wiki/Audi_Type_P" title="Audi Type P">the "four"</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a> engine) models were manufactured. Audi cars of that era were luxurious cars equipped with special bodywork.</p>
<p>In 1932, Audi merged with <a href="/wiki/Horch" title="Horch">Horch</a>, DKW, and <a href="/wiki/Wanderer_(car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wanderer (car)">Wanderer</a>, to form <a href="/wiki/Auto_Union" title="Auto Union">Auto Union</a> AG, <a href="/wiki/Chemnitz" title="Chemnitz">Chemnitz</a>. It was during this period that the company offered the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Front" title="Audi Front">Audi Front</a> that became the first European car to combine a six-cylinder engine with front-wheel drive. It used a powertrain shared with the Wanderer, but turned 180-degrees, so that the drive shaft faced the front.</p>
<p>Before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Auto Union used the four interlinked rings that make up the Audi badge today, representing these four brands. This badge was used, however, only on Auto Union racing cars in that period while the member companies used their own names and emblems. The technological development became more and more concentrated and some Audi models were propelled by Horch or Wanderer built engines.</p>
<p>Reflecting the economic pressures of the time, Auto Union concentrated increasingly on smaller cars through the 1930s, so that by 1938 the company's DKW brand accounted for 17.9% of the German car market, while Audi held only 0.1%. After the final few Audis were delivered in 1939 the "Audi" name disappeared completely from the new car market for more than two decades.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg/220px-IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg/330px-IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg/440px-IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1497" data-file-height="1326" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IFA_F9_front_20040924.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/IFA_F9" title="IFA F9">IFA F9</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like most German manufacturing, at the onset of World War II the Auto Union plants were retooled for military production, and were a target for allied bombing during the war which left them damaged.</p>
<p>Overrun by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet Army</a> in 1945, on the orders of the Soviet Union military administration the factories were dismantled as part of <a href="/wiki/War_reparations" title="War reparations">war reparations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle6_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle6-22">[22]</a></sup> Following this, the company's entire assets were expropriated without compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle6_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle6-22">[22]</a></sup> On 17 August 1948, Auto Union AG of Chemnitz was deleted from the commercial register.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle4_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle4-21">[21]</a></sup> These actions had the effect of liquidating Germany's Auto Union AG. The remains of the Audi plant of Zwickau became the <a href="/wiki/Volkseigener_Betrieb" title="Volkseigener Betrieb">VEB</a> (for "People Owned Enterprise") <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automobilwerk_Zwickau" class="extiw" title="de:Automobilwerk Zwickau">Automobilwerk Zwickau</a> or AWZ (in English: Automobile Works Zwickau).</p>
<p>With no prospect of continuing production in Soviet controlled East Germany, Auto Union executives began the process of relocating what was left of the company to <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. A site was chosen in <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt" title="Ingolstadt">Ingolstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> to start a spare parts operation in late 1945, which would eventually serve as the headquarters of the reformed Auto Union in 1949.</p>
<p>The former Audi factory in Zwickau restarted assembly of the pre-war-models in 1949. These DKW models were renamed to <a href="/wiki/IFA_F8" class="mw-redirect" title="IFA F8">IFA F8</a> and <a href="/wiki/IFA_F9" title="IFA F9">IFA F9</a> and were similar to the West German versions. West and East German models were equipped with the traditional and renowned DKW two-stroke engines. The Zwickau plant manufactured the infamous <a href="/wiki/Trabant" title="Trabant">Trabant</a> until 1991, when it came under Volkswagen control—effectively bringing it under the same umbrella as Audi since 1945.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Auto_Union_unit">New Auto Union unit</span></h3>
<p>A new West German headquartered Auto Union was launched in Ingolstadt, Bavaria with loans from the Bavarian state government and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> aid.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle6_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle6-22">[22]</a></sup> The reformed company was launched 3 September 1949 and continued DKW's tradition of producing front-wheel drive vehicles with two-stroke engines.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle6_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle6-22">[22]</a></sup> This included production of a small but sturdy 125&#160;cc motorcycle and a DKW delivery van, the <a href="/wiki/DKW_Schnellaster" title="DKW Schnellaster">DKW F89 L</a> at Ingolstadt. The Ingolstadt site was large, consisting of an extensive complex of formerly military buildings which was suitable for administration as well as vehicle warehousing and distribution, but at this stage there was at Ingolstadt no dedicated plant suitable for mass production of automobiles: for manufacturing the company's <a href="/wiki/DKW_F89" title="DKW F89">first post-war mass-market passenger car</a> plant capacity in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> was rented from <a href="/wiki/Rheinmetall" title="Rheinmetall">Rheinmetall-Borsig</a>. It was only ten years later, after the company had attracted an investor that funds became available for construction of major car plant at the Ingolstadt head office site.</p>
<p>In 1958, in response to pressure from <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Flick" title="Friedrich Flick">Friedrich Flick</a>, then their largest single shareholder,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daimler-Benz" title="Daimler-Benz">Daimler-Benz</a> took an 87% holding in the Auto Union company, and this was increased to a 100% holding in 1959. However, small two-stroke cars were not the focus of Daimler-Benz's interests, and while the early 1960s saw major investment in new Mercedes models and in a state of the art factory for Auto Union's, the company's aging model range at this time did not benefit from the economic boom of the early 1960s to the same extent as competitor manufacturers such as <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a>. The decision to dispose of the Auto Union business was based on its lack of profitability.<sup id="cite_ref-Motor197107_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motor197107-24">[24]</a></sup> Ironically, by the time they sold the business, it also included a large new factory and near production-ready modern four-stroke engine, which would enable the Auto Union business, under a new owner, to embark on a period of profitable growth, now producing not Auto Unions or DKWs, but using the "Audi" name, resurrected in 1965 after a 25-year gap.</p>
<p>In 1964, Volkswagen acquired a 50% holding in the business, which included the new factory in Ingolstadt, the DKW and Audi brands along with the rights to the new engine design which had been funded by Daimler-Benz, who in return retained the dormant Horch trademark and the Düsseldorf factory which became a Mercedes-Benz van assembly plant. Eighteen months later, Volkswagen bought complete control of Ingolstadt, and by 1966 were using the spare capacity of the Ingolstadt plant to assemble an additional 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Type_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Volkswagen Type 1">Volkswagen Beetles</a> per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Motor19710724_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motor19710724-25">[25]</a></sup> Two-stroke engines became less popular during the 1960s as customers were more attracted to the smoother four-stroke engines. In September 1965, the <a href="/wiki/DKW_F102" title="DKW F102">DKW F102</a> was fitted with a four-stroke engine and a <a href="/wiki/Facelift_(automotive)" title="Facelift (automotive)">facelift</a> for the car's front and rear. Volkswagen dumped the DKW brand because of its associations with two-stroke technology, and having classified the model internally as the <a href="/wiki/Audi_F103" title="Audi F103">F103</a>, sold it simply as the "Audi." Later developments of the model were named after their horsepower ratings and sold as the Audi 60, 75, 80, and Super 90, selling until 1972. Initially, Volkswagen was hostile to the idea of Auto Union as a standalone entity producing its own models having acquired the company merely to boost its own production capacity through the Ingolstadt assembly plant - to the point where Volkswagen executives ordered that the Auto Union name and flags bearing the four rings were removed from the factory buildings. Then VW chief <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Nordhoff" title="Heinrich Nordhoff">Heinz Nordhoff</a> explicitly forbade Auto Union from any further product development. Fearing that the Volkswagen had no long term ambition for the Audi brand, Auto Union engineers under the leadership of Ludwig Kraus developed the first <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a> in secret, without Nordhoff's knowledge. When presented with a finished prototype, Nordhoff was so impressed he authorised the car for production, which when launched in 1968, went on to be a huge success. With this, the resurrection of the Audi brand was now complete, this being followed by the first generation <a href="/wiki/Audi_80#B1_.281972.E2.80.9378.29" title="Audi 80">Audi 80</a> in 1972, which would in turn provide a template for VW's new front-wheel-drive water-cooled range which debuted from the mid-1970s onward.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035,_Wolfsburg,_VW_Autowerk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035%2C_Wolfsburg%2C_VW_Autowerk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="501" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F038791-0035,_Wolfsburg,_VW_Autowerk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 80</a> <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wolfsburg" title="Wolfsburg">Wolfsburg</a>, 1973</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1969, Auto Union merged with <a href="/wiki/NSU_Motorenwerke_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="NSU Motorenwerke AG">NSU</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Neckarsulm" title="Neckarsulm">Neckarsulm</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>. In the 1950s, NSU had been the world's largest manufacturer of motorcycles, but had moved on to produce small cars like the <a href="/wiki/NSU_Prinz" title="NSU Prinz">NSU Prinz</a>, the TT and TTS versions of which are still popular as vintage race cars. NSU then focused on new rotary engines based on the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Felix_Wankel" title="Felix Wankel">Felix Wankel</a>. In 1967, the new <a href="/wiki/NSU_Ro_80" title="NSU Ro 80">NSU Ro 80</a> was a car well ahead of its time in technical details such as aerodynamics, light weight, and safety. However, teething problems with the rotary engines put an end to the independence of NSU. The Neckarsulm plant is now used to produce the larger Audi models <a href="/wiki/Audi_A6" title="Audi A6">A6</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">A8</a>. The Neckarsulm factory is also home of the "<a href="/wiki/Quattro_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="Quattro GmbH">quattro GmbH</a>" (from November 2016 "<a href="/wiki/Audi_Sport_GmbH" title="Audi Sport GmbH">Audi Sport GmbH</a>"), a subsidiary responsible for development and production of Audi high-performance models: the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8_(road_car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi R8 (road car)">R8</a> and the <b>"RS"</b> model range.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span></h3>
<p>The new merged company was incorporated on 1 January 1969 and was known as <b>Audi NSU Auto Union AG</b>, with its headquarters based at NSU's Neckarsulm plant, and saw the emergence of Audi as a separate brand for the first time since the pre-war era. Volkswagen introduced the Audi brand to the United States for the 1970 model year. That same year, the mid-sized car that NSU had been working on, the <a href="/wiki/VW_K70" class="mw-redirect" title="VW K70">K70</a>, originally intended to slot between the rear-engined Prinz models and the futuristic <a href="/wiki/NSU_Ro_80" title="NSU Ro 80">NSU Ro 80</a>, was instead launched as a Volkswagen.</p>
<p>After the launch of the <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a> of 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 80</a>/Fox (which formed the basis for the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Passat" title="Volkswagen Passat">Volkswagen Passat</a>) followed in 1972 and the <a href="/wiki/Audi_50" title="Audi 50">Audi 50</a> (later rebadged as the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Polo" title="Volkswagen Polo">Volkswagen Polo</a>) in 1974. The Audi 50 was a seminal design because it was the first incarnation of the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Golf/Polo</a> concept, one that led to a hugely successful world car. Ultimately, the Audi 80 and 100 (progenitors of the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">A4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_A6" title="Audi A6">A6</a>, respectively) became the company's biggest sellers, whilst little investment was made in the fading NSU range; the <a href="/wiki/NSU_Prinz" title="NSU Prinz">Prinz</a> models were dropped in 1973 whilst the fatally flawed <a href="/wiki/NSU_Ro80" class="mw-redirect" title="NSU Ro80">NSU Ro80</a> went out of production in 1977, spelling the effective end of the NSU brand. Production of the Audi 100 had been steadily moved from Ingolstadt to Neckarsulm as the 1970s had progressed, any by the appearance of the second generation C2 version in 1976, all production was now at the former NSU plant. Neckarsulm from that point onward would produce Audi's higher end models.</p>
<p>The Audi image at this time was a conservative one, and so, a proposal from chassis engineer <a href="/w/index.php?title=J%C3%B6rg_Bensinger&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jörg Bensinger (page does not exist)">Jörg Bensinger</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> was accepted to develop the <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> technology in <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Iltis" title="Volkswagen Iltis">Iltis</a> military vehicle for an Audi performance car and <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rally</a> racing car. The performance car, introduced in 1980, was named the "<a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Audi Quattro</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Turbo" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbo">turbocharged</a> coupé which was also the first German large-scale production vehicle to feature permanent <a href="/wiki/All-wheel_drive" title="All-wheel drive">all-wheel drive</a> through a centre <a href="/wiki/Differential_(mechanical_device)" title="Differential (mechanical device)">differential</a>. Commonly referred to as the "Ur-Quattro" (the "<a href="/wiki/Proto-World_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-World language">Ur-</a>" prefix is a German <a href="/wiki/Augmentative" title="Augmentative">augmentative</a> used, in this case, to mean "original" and is also applied to the first generation of Audi's <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4" title="Audi S4">S4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">S6</a> Sport Saloons, as in "UrS4" and "UrS6"), few of these vehicles were produced (all hand-built by a single team), but the model was a great success in rallying. Prominent wins proved the viability of all-wheel drive racecars, and the Audi name became associated with advances in automotive technology.</p>
<p>In 1985, with the Auto Union and NSU brands effectively dead, the company's official name was now shortened to simply <b>Audi AG</b>. At the same time the company's headquarters moved back to Ingolstadt and two new wholly owned subsidiaries; <i>Auto Union GmbH</i> and <i>NSU GmbH</i>, were formed to own and manage the historical trademarks and intellectual property of the original constituent companies (the exception being Horch, which had been retained by Daimler-Benz after the VW takeover), and to operate Audi's heritage operations.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg/220px-Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg/330px-Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg/440px-Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="663" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Quattro_20V_-_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Audi Quattro</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1986, as the Passat-based <a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 80</a> was beginning to develop a kind of "grandfather's car" image, the <i>type 89</i> was introduced. This completely new development sold extremely well. However, its modern and dynamic exterior belied the low performance of its base engine, and its base package was quite spartan (even the passenger-side mirror was an option.) In 1987, Audi put forward a new and very elegant <a href="/wiki/Audi_90" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi 90">Audi 90</a>, which had a much superior set of standard features. In the early 1990s, sales began to slump for the Audi 80 series, and some basic construction problems started to surface.</p>
<p>In the early part of the 21st century, Audi set forth on a German racetrack to claim and maintain several world records, such as top speed endurance. This effort was in-line with the company's heritage from the 1930s racing era <a href="/wiki/Silver_Arrows" title="Silver Arrows">Silver Arrows</a>.</p>
<p>Through the early 1990s, Audi began to shift its target market upscale to compete against German automakers <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>. This began with the release of the <a href="/wiki/Audi_V8" title="Audi V8">Audi V8</a> in 1990. It was essentially a new engine fitted to the Audi 100/200, but with noticeable bodywork differences. Most obvious was the new grille that was now incorporated in the bonnet.</p>
<p>By 1991, Audi had the four-cylinder Audi 80, the 5-cylinder <a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 90</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a>, the turbocharged <a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 200</a> and the Audi V8. There was also a coupe version of the 80/90 with both 4- and 5-cylinder engines.</p>
<p>Although the five-cylinder engine was a successful and robust powerplant, it was still a little too different for the target market. With the introduction of an all-new Audi 100 in 1992, Audi introduced a 2.8L <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6 engine</a>. This engine was also fitted to a face-lifted Audi 80 (all 80 and 90 models were now badged 80 except for the USA), giving this model a choice of four-, five-, and six-cylinder engines, in <a href="/wiki/Saloon_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saloon (automobile)">Saloon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">Coupé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabriolet_(automobile)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabriolet (automobile)">Cabriolet</a> body styles.</p>
<p>The five-cylinder was soon dropped as a major engine choice; however, a <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbocharged</a> 230&#160;hp (170&#160;kW) version remained. The engine, initially fitted to the 200 quattro 20V of 1991, was a derivative of the engine fitted to the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro#Sport_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Sport Quattro</a>. It was fitted to the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Coup%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi Coupé">Audi Coupé</a>, and named the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S2" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi S2">S2</a> and also to the Audi 100 body, and named the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4" title="Audi S4">S4</a>. These two models were the beginning of the mass-produced <a href="/wiki/Audi_S_models" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi S models">S series</a> of performance cars.</p>
<p>In November 2016, Audi expressed an intention to establish an assembly factory in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, with the company's local partner acquiring land for a plant in <a href="/wiki/Korangi_Creek_Industrial_Park" title="Korangi Creek Industrial Park">Korangi Creek Industrial Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>. Approval of the plan would lead to an investment of $30 million in the new plant.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_5000_unintended_acceleration_allegations">Audi 5000 unintended acceleration allegations</span></h3>
<p>Sales in the United States fell after a series of recalls from 1982 to 1987 of <a href="/wiki/Audi_5000" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi 5000">Audi 5000</a> models<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup> associated with reported incidents of <a href="/wiki/Sudden_unintended_acceleration" title="Sudden unintended acceleration">sudden unintended acceleration</a> linked to six deaths and 700 accidents.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup> At the time, NHTSA was investigating 50 car models from 20 manufacturers for sudden surges of power.<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i> report aired 23 November 1986,<sup id="cite_ref-debacle_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debacle-30">[30]</a></sup> featuring interviews with six people who had sued Audi after reporting unintended acceleration, showing an Audi 5000 ostensibly suffering a problem when the brake pedal was pushed.<sup id="cite_ref-huber_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huber-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Subsequent investigation revealed that <i>60 Minutes</i> had engineered the failure – fitting a canister of compressed air on the passenger-side floor, linked via a hose to a hole drilled into the transmission.<sup id="cite_ref-debacle_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debacle-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mint_Audi_100_(1982-91)_(10629216834).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg/220px-Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg/330px-Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg/440px-Mint_Audi_100_%281982-91%29_%2810629216834%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4080" data-file-height="2153" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mint_Audi_100_(1982-91)_(10629216834).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Audi_100" title="Audi 100">Audi 100</a> C3, sold as the <a href="/wiki/Audi_5000" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi 5000">Audi 5000</a> in the U.S.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi contended, prior to findings by outside investigators,<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed-29">[29]</a></sup> that the problems were caused by driver error, specifically pedal misapplication.<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed-29">[29]</a></sup> Subsequently, the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) concluded that the majority of unintended acceleration cases, including all the ones that prompted the <i>60 Minutes</i> report, were caused by driver error such as confusion of pedals.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> CBS did not acknowledge the test results of involved government agencies, but did acknowledge the similar results of another study.<sup id="cite_ref-huber_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huber-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a review study published in 2012, NHTSA summarized its past findings about the Audi unintended acceleration problems: "Once an unintended acceleration had begun, in the Audi 5000, due to a failure in the idle-stabilizer system (producing an initial acceleration of 0.3g), pedal misapplication resulting from panic, confusion, or unfamiliarity with the Audi 5000 contributed to the severity of the incident."<sup id="cite_ref-nhtsa2012_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhtsa2012-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>This summary is consistent with the conclusions of NHTSA's most technical analysis at the time: "Audi idle-stabilization systems were prone to defects which resulted in excessive idle speeds and brief unanticipated accelerations of up to 0.3g [which is similar in magnitude to an emergency stop in a subway car]. These accelerations could not be the sole cause of [(long-duration) sudden acceleration incidents (SAI)], but might have triggered some SAIs by startling the driver.<sup id="cite_ref-audi1988_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-audi1988-35">[35]</a></sup> The defective idle-stabilization system performed a type of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_throttle_control" title="Electronic throttle control">electronic throttle control</a>. Significantly: multiple "intermittent malfunctions of the electronic control unit were observed and recorded ... and [were also observed and] reported by Transport Canada."<sup id="cite_ref-audi1988_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-audi1988-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a series of recall campaigns, Audi made several modifications; the first adjusted the distance between the brake and accelerator pedal on automatic-transmission models.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup> Later repairs, of 250,000 cars dating back to 1978, added a device requiring the driver to press the brake pedal before shifting out of park.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup> A legacy of the Audi 5000 and other reported cases of sudden unintended acceleration are intricate <a href="/wiki/Gear_stick" title="Gear stick">gear stick</a> patterns and brake <a href="/wiki/Interlock" class="mw-redirect" title="Interlock">interlock</a> mechanisms to prevent inadvertent shifting into forward or reverse. It is unclear how the defects in the idle-stabilization system were addressed.</p>
<p>Audi's U.S. sales, which had reached 74,061 in 1985, dropped to 12,283 in 1991 and remained level for three years.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup> – with resale values falling dramatically.<sup id="cite_ref-warranty_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warranty-36">[36]</a></sup> Audi subsequently offered increased warranty protection<sup id="cite_ref-warranty_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warranty-36">[36]</a></sup> and renamed the affected models – with the <i>5000</i> becoming the <i>100</i> and <i>200</i> in 1989<sup id="cite_ref-renamed_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renamed-29">[29]</a></sup> – and only reached the same sales levels again by model year 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2010 <i>BusinessWeek</i> article – outlining possible parallels between Audi's experience and <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%932010_Toyota_vehicle_recalls" class="mw-redirect" title="2009–2010 Toyota vehicle recalls">2009–2010 Toyota vehicle recalls</a> – noted a class-action lawsuit filed in 1987 by about 7,500 Audi 5000-model owners remains unsettled and is currently being contested in county court in Chicago after appeals at the Illinois state and U.S. federal levels.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_28-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_introductions">Model introductions</span></h3>
<p>In the mid-to-late 1990s, Audi introduced new technologies including the use of aluminum construction. Produced from 1999 to 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A2" title="Audi A2">Audi A2</a> was a futuristic super mini, born from the Al2 concept, with many features that helped regain consumer confidence, like the aluminium <a href="/wiki/Space_frame" title="Space frame">space frame</a>, which was a first in production car design. In the A2 Audi further expanded their TDI technology through the use of frugal three-cylinder engines. The A2 was extremely aerodynamic and was designed around a <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnel</a>. The Audi A2 was criticised for its high price and was never really a sales success but it planted Audi as a cutting-edge manufacturer. The model, a <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_A-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz A-Class">Mercedes-Benz A-Class</a> competitor, sold relatively well in Europe. However, the A2 was discontinued in 2005 and Audi decided not to develop an immediate replacement.</p>
<p>The next major model change came in 1995 when the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a> replaced the <a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 80</a>. The new nomenclature scheme was applied to the Audi 100 to become the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A6" title="Audi A6">Audi A6</a> (with a minor facelift). This also meant the S4 became the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S6" title="Audi S6">S6</a> and a new S4 was introduced in the A4 body. The S2 was discontinued. The <a href="/wiki/Audi_Cabriolet" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi Cabriolet">Audi Cabriolet</a> continued on (based on the Audi 80 platform) until 1999, gaining the engine upgrades along the way. A new <a href="/wiki/Audi_A3" title="Audi A3">A3</a> <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">hatchback</a> model (sharing the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk4" title="Volkswagen Golf Mk4">Volkswagen Golf Mk4</a>'s platform) was introduced to the range in 1996, and the radical <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">Audi TT</a> <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9" title="Coupé">coupé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roadster_(automobile)" title="Roadster (automobile)">roadster</a> were debuted in 1998 based on the same underpinnings.</p>
<p>The engines available throughout the range were now a 1.4&#160;L, 1.6&#160;L and 1.8&#160;L four-cylinder, 1.8&#160;L four-cylinder turbo, 2.6&#160;L and 2.8&#160;L <a href="/wiki/V6_engine" title="V6 engine">V6</a>, 2.2&#160;L turbo-charged five-cylinder and the 4.2&#160;L <a href="/wiki/V8_engine" title="V8 engine">V8 engine</a>. The V6s were replaced by new 2.4&#160;L and 2.8&#160;L 30V V6s in 1998, with marked improvement in power, torque and smoothness. Further engines were added along the way, including a 3.7&#160;L V8 and 6.0&#160;L <a href="/wiki/W12_engine" title="W12 engine">W12 engine</a> for the A8.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_AG_today">Audi AG today</span></h3>
<p>Audi's sales grew strongly in the 2000s, with deliveries to customers increasing from 653,000 in 2000 to 1,003,000 in 2008. The largest sales increases came from Eastern Europe (+19.3%), Africa (+17.2%) and the Middle East (+58.5%). China in particular has become a key market, representing 108,000 out of 705,000 cars delivered in the first three quarters of 2009. One factor for its popularity in China is that Audis have become the car of choice for purchase by the Chinese government for officials, and purchases by the government are responsible for 20% of its sales in China.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> As of late 2009, Audi's operating profit of €1.17-billion ($1.85-billion) made it the biggest contributor to parent Volkswagen Group's nine-month operating profit of €1.5-billion, while the other marques in Group such as Bentley and SEAT had suffered considerable losses.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> May 2011 saw record sales for Audi of America with the new <a href="/wiki/Audi_A7" title="Audi A7">Audi A7</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_A3" title="Audi A3">Audi A3</a> TDI Clean Diesel.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In May 2012, Audi reported a 10% increase in its sales—from 408 units to 480 in the last year alone.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audi manufactures vehicles in seven plants around the world, some of which are shared with other VW Group marques<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> although many sub-assemblies such as engines and transmissions are manufactured within other Volkswagen Group plants.</p>
<p>Audi's two principal assembly plants are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt" title="Ingolstadt">Ingolstadt</a>, Opened by Auto Union in 1964, (A3, A4, A5, Q5)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neckarsulm" title="Neckarsulm">Neckarsulm</a>, Acquired from NSU in 1969 (A4, A6, A7, A8, R8 &amp; all RS variants)</li>
</ul>
<p>Outside of Germany, Audi produces vehicles at:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aurangabad,_Maharashtra" title="Aurangabad, Maharashtra">Aurangabad</a>, India since 2006</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, Slovakia, shared with Volkswagen, SEAT, Škoda and Porsche (Q7)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, Belgium, acquired from Volkswagen in 2007 (A1)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Changchun" title="Changchun">Changchun</a>, China since 1995</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gy%C5%91r" title="Győr">Győr</a>, Hungary, (TT and some A3 variants)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Indonesia since 2011</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martorell" title="Martorell">Martorell</a>, Spain shared with SEAT and Volkswagen (Q3)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Chiapa" title="San José Chiapa">San José Chiapa</a>, Mexico (Q5)</li>
</ul>
<p>In September 2012, Audi announced the construction of its first North American manufacturing plant in <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>, Mexico. This plant is expected to be operative in 2016 and produce the second generation Q5.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2002 up to 2003, Audi headed the Audi Brand Group, a subdivision of the Volkswagen Group's Automotive Division consisting of Audi, Lamborghini and SEAT, that was focused on sporty values, with the marques' product vehicles and performance being under the higher responsibility of the Audi brand.</p>
<p>On January 2014, Audi, along with the <a href="/wiki/Wireless_Power_Consortium" title="Wireless Power Consortium">Wireless Power Consortium</a>, operated a booth which demonstrated a phone compartment using the <a href="/wiki/Qi_(standard)" title="Qi (standard)">Qi</a> <a href="/wiki/Open_standard" title="Open standard">open</a> <a href="/wiki/Interface_standard" title="Interface standard">interface standard</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> (CES).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In May, most of the Audi dealers in UK falsely claimed that the Audi A7, A8, and R8 were Euro NCAP safety tested, all achieving five out of five stars. In fact none were tested.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Audi admitted that at least 2.1 million Audi cars had been involved in the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_emissions_testing_scandal" class="mw-redirect" title="Volkswagen emissions testing scandal">Volkswagen emissions testing scandal</a> in which software installed in the cars manipulated emissions data to fool regulators and allow the cars to pollute at higher than government-mandated levels. The A1, A3, A4, A5, A6, TT, Q3 and Q5 models were implicated in the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Audi promised to quickly find a technical solution and upgrade the cars so they can function within emissions regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Ulrich Hackenberg, the head of research and development at Audi, was suspended in relation to the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Despite widespread media coverage about the scandal through the month of September, Audi reported that U.S. sales for the month had increased by 16.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2015, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency implicated the 3-liter diesel engine versions of the 2016 Audi A6 Quattro, A7 Quattro, A8, A8L and the Q5 as further models that had emissions regulation defeat-device software installed.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Thus, these models emitted nitrogen oxide at up to nine times the legal limit when the car detected that it was not hooked up to emissions testing equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bodyshells">Bodyshells</span></h3>
<p>Audi produces 100% <a href="/wiki/Galvanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Galvanisation">galvanised</a> <a href="/wiki/Automobiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobiles">cars</a> to prevent <a href="/wiki/Corrosion" title="Corrosion">corrosion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and was the first mass-market vehicle to do so, following introduction of the process by <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a>, c. 1975. Along with other precautionary measures, the full-body <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> coating has proved to be very effective in preventing rust. The body's resulting durability even surpassed Audi's own expectations, causing the manufacturer to extend its original 10-year <a href="/wiki/Warranty" title="Warranty">warranty</a> against corrosion perforation to currently 12 years (except for aluminium bodies which do not rust).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_frame">Space frame</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_(160)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_%28160%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3630" data-file-height="1640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_R8_-_Flickr_-_Alexandre_Pr%C3%A9vot_(160)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Audi R8 uses Audi Space Frame technology</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi introduced a new series of vehicles in the mid-1990s and continues to pursue new technology and high performance. An all-aluminium car was brought forward by Audi, and in 1994 the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a> was launched, which introduced aluminium <a href="/wiki/Space_frame" title="Space frame">space frame</a> technology (called <i>Audi Space Frame</i> or ASF) which saves weight and improves torsion rigidity compared to a conventional steel frame. Prior to that effort, Audi used examples of the Type 44 chassis fabricated out of aluminium as test-beds for the technique. The disadvantage of the aluminium frame is that it is very expensive to repair and requires a specialized aluminium bodyshop.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The weight reduction is somewhat offset by the <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel_drive_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quattro (four-wheel drive system)">quattro</a> <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> system which is standard in most markets. Nonetheless, the A8 is usually the lightest all-wheel drive car in the full-size luxury segment, also having best-in-class fuel economy.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Audi_A2" title="Audi A2">Audi A2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">Audi TT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8_(road_car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi R8 (road car)">Audi R8</a> also use Audi Space Frame designs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drivetrains">Drivetrains</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Layout">Layout</span></h4>
<p>For most of its lineup (excluding the A3, A1, and TT models), Audi has not adopted the transverse engine layout which is typically found in economy cars (such as Peugeot and Citroën), since that would limit the type and power of engines that can be installed. To be able to mount powerful engines (such as a V8 engine in the <a href="/wiki/Audi_S4" title="Audi S4">Audi S4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_RS4" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi RS4">Audi RS4</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/W12_engine" title="W12 engine">W12 engine</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8L W12</a>), Audi has usually engineered its more expensive cars with a <a href="/wiki/Longitudinal_engine" title="Longitudinal engine">longitudinally</a> <a href="/wiki/Front-engine_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Front-engine design">front-mounted engine</a>, in an "overhung" position, over the front wheels in front of the axle line - this layout dates back to the DKW and Auto Union saloons from the 1950s. But while this allows for the easy adoption of all-wheel drive, it goes against the ideal 50:50 weight distribution.</p>
<p>In all its post <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>-era models, Audi has firmly refused to adopt the traditional <a href="/wiki/Rear-wheel_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Rear-wheel drive">rear-wheel drive</a> layout favored by its two archrivals <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, favoring either <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a> or <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">all-wheel drive</a>. The majority of Audi's lineup in the United States features all-wheel drive standard on most of its expensive vehicles (only the entry-level trims of the A4 and A6 are available with front-wheel drive), in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> whose lineup treats all-wheel drive as an option. BMW did not offer all-wheel drive on its V8-powered cars (as opposed to crossover SUVs) until the 2010 BMW 7 Series and 2011 BMW 5 Series, while the Audi A8 has had all-wheel drive available/standard since the 1990s. Regarding high-performance variants, <a href="/wiki/Audi_S_and_RS_models" title="Audi S and RS models">Audi S and RS models</a> have always had all-wheel drive, unlike their direct rivals from <a href="/wiki/BMW_M" title="BMW M">BMW M</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-AMG" title="Mercedes-AMG">Mercedes-AMG</a> whose cars are rear-wheel drive only (although their performance crossover SUVs are all-wheel drive).</p>
<p>Audi has recently applied the <i><a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel_drive_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quattro (four-wheel drive system)">quattro</a></i> badge to models such as the A3 and TT which do not use the <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">Torsen</a>-based system as in prior years with a mechanical center differential, but with the <a href="/wiki/Haldex_Traction" title="Haldex Traction">Haldex Traction</a> electro-mechanical clutch AWD system.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines">Engines</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Volkswagen_W12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Volkswagen_W12.jpg/170px-Volkswagen_W12.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Volkswagen_W12.jpg/255px-Volkswagen_W12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Volkswagen_W12.jpg/340px-Volkswagen_W12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Volkswagen_W12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> W12 engine from the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Phaeton" title="Volkswagen Phaeton">Volkswagen Phaeton W12</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Audi_vehicles#Production_model_engines" title="List of Audi vehicles">List of Audi vehicles §&#160;Production model engines</a></div>
<p>Prior to the introduction of the Audi 80 and Audi 50 in 1972 and 1974, respectively, Audi had led the development of the <i>EA111</i> and <i>EA827</i> <a href="/wiki/Straight-four_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Straight-four engine">inline-four</a> engine families. These new power units underpinned the water-cooled revival of parent company Volkswagen (in the Polo, Golf, Passat and Scirocco), whilst the many derivatives and descendants of these two basic engine designs have appeared in every generation of VW Group vehicles right up to the present day.</p>
<p>In the 1980s, Audi, along with Volvo, was the champion of the <a href="/wiki/Straight-five_engine" title="Straight-five engine">inline-five</a> cylinder, <a href="/wiki/Engine_displacement" title="Engine displacement">2.1/2.2 L</a> engine as a longer-lasting alternative to more traditional six-cylinder engines. This engine was used not only in production cars but also in their race cars. The 2.1&#160;L inline five-cylinder engine was used as a base for the <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rally cars</a> in the 1980s, providing well over 400 horsepower (300 kilowatts) after modification. Before 1990, there were engines produced with a displacement between 2.0&#160;L and 2.3&#160;L. This range of engine capacity allowed for both fuel economy and power.</p>
<p>For the ultra-luxury version of its <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a> fullsize luxury flagship sedan, the Audi A8L W12, Audi uses the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Volkswagen_Group_petrol_engines#W12" title="List of Volkswagen Group petrol engines">W12 engine</a> instead of the conventional <a href="/wiki/V12_engine" title="V12 engine">V12 engine</a> favored by rivals Mercedes-Benz and BMW. The W12 engine configuration (also known as a "WR12") is created by forming two imaginary narrow-angle 15° <a href="/wiki/VR6_engine" title="VR6 engine">VR6 engines</a> at an angle of 72°, and the narrow angle of each set of cylinders allows just two <a href="/wiki/Overhead_camshaft" title="Overhead camshaft">overhead camshafts</a> to drive each pair of banks, so just four are needed in total.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoZine_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutoZine-55">[55]</a></sup> The advantage of the W12 engine is its compact packaging, allowing Audi to build a 12-cylinder sedan with all-wheel drive, whereas a conventional <a href="/wiki/V12_engine" title="V12 engine">V12 engine</a> could only have a rear-wheel drive configuration as it would have no space in the engine bay for a differential and other components required to power the front wheels. In fact, the 6.0&#160;L W12 in the Audi A8L W12 is smaller in overall dimensions than the 4.2&#160;L V8 that powers the Audi A8 4.2 variants.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The 2011 Audi A8 debuted a revised 6.3-litre version of the W12 (WR12) engine with 500&#160;PS (370&#160;kW; 490&#160;hp).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_Stratified_Injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</span></h4>
<p>New models of the A3, A4, A6 and A8 have been introduced, with the ageing 1.8-litre engine now having been replaced by new <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">Fuel Stratified Injection</a> (FSI) engines. Nearly every petroleum burning model in the range now incorporates this fuel-saving technology.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG/220px-2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG/330px-2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG/440px-2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1458" data-file-height="1096" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_Audi_R8_Engine.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
V8 FSI engine</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Direct-Shift_Gearbox">Direct-Shift Gearbox</span></h4>
<p>At the turn of the century, Volkswagen introduced the <a href="/wiki/Direct-Shift_Gearbox" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct-Shift Gearbox">Direct-Shift Gearbox</a> (DSG), a type of <a href="/wiki/Dual_clutch_transmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual clutch transmission">dual clutch transmission</a>. It is an automated <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_transmission" title="Semi-automatic transmission">semi-automatic transmission</a>, drivable like a conventional <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a>. Based on the gearbox found in the Group B S1, the system includes dual electrohydraulically controlled <a href="/wiki/Clutch" title="Clutch">clutches</a> instead of a <a href="/wiki/Torque_converter" title="Torque converter">torque converter</a>. This is implemented in some <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">VW Golfs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A3" title="Audi A3">Audi A3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">TT</a> models where DSG is called S-tronic.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LED_daytime_running_lights">LED daytime running lights</span></h3>
<p>Beginning in 2005, Audi has implemented white <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LED</a> technology as <a href="/wiki/Daytime_running_light" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytime running light">daytime running lights</a> (DRL) in their products. The distinctive shape of the DRLs has become a trademark of sorts. LEDs were first introduced on the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8#D3" title="Audi A8">Audi A8 W12</a>, the world's first production car to have LED DRLs,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and have since spread throughout the entire model range. The LEDs are present on some Audi <a href="/wiki/Billboard" title="Billboard">billboards</a>.</p>
<p>Since 2010, Audi has also offered the <a href="/wiki/LED_headlamp" class="mw-redirect" title="LED headlamp">LED technology in low- and high-beam headlights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/220px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/330px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/440px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3526" data-file-height="2350" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multi_Media_Interface">Multi Media Interface</span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>contains content that is written like <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_soapbox_or_means_of_promotion" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">an advertisement</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Audi&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spam" title="Wikipedia:Spam">promotional content</a> and inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, and by adding encyclopedic content written from a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutral point of view</a>.</span> <small><i>(January 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_TT_2014_(13558812864).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg/220px-Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg/330px-Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg/440px-Audi_TT_2014_%2813558812864%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_TT_2014_(13558812864).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Multi Media Interface-Menu on <a href="/wiki/Audi_virtual_cockpit" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi virtual cockpit">Audi virtual cockpit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT_Mk3" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi TT Mk3">Audi TT Mk3</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starting with the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a>, Audi has used a centralised control interface for its on-board <a href="/wiki/Infotainment" title="Infotainment">infotainment</a> systems, called <a href="/wiki/Multi_Media_Interface" title="Multi Media Interface">Multi Media Interface</a> (MMI). This came amid criticism of BMW's <a href="/wiki/IDrive" title="IDrive">iDrive</a> control. It is essentially a rotating control knob and 'segment' buttons – designed to control all in-car entertainment devices (radio, CD changer, iPod, TV tuner), satellite navigation, heating and ventilation, and other car controls with a screen. MMI was widely reported to be a considerable improvement on BMW's iDrive, although BMW has since made their iDrive more user-friendly.</p>
<p>The availability of MMI has gradually filtered down the Audi lineup, and following its introduction on the third generation A3 in 2011, MMI is now available across the entire range. It has been generally well received, as it requires less menu-surfing with its segment buttons around a central knob, along with 'main function' direct access buttons – with shortcuts to the radio or phone functions. The colour screen is mounted on the upright dashboard, and on the A4 (new), A5, A6, A8, and Q7, the controls are mounted horizontally.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synthetic_Diesel">Synthetic Diesel</span></h3>
<p>Audi has assisted with technology to produce <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_diesel" class="mw-redirect" title="Synthetic diesel">synthetic diesel</a> from water and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logistics">Logistics</span></h3>
<p>Audi uses scanning gloves for parts registration during assembly, and automatic robots to transfer cars from factory to rail cars.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_vehicles">Electric vehicles</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Audi_vehicles#Concept_models" title="List of Audi vehicles">List of Audi vehicles §&#160;Concept models</a></div>
<p>Audi is planning an alliance with the Japanese electronics giant <a href="/wiki/Sanyo" title="Sanyo">Sanyo</a> to develop a pilot hybrid electric project for the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>. The alliance could result in Sanyo batteries and other electronic components being used in future models of the Volkswagen Group.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Concept electric vehicles unveiled to date include the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A1" title="Audi A1">Audi A1</a> Sportback Concept,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a> TDI Concept E,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and the fully electric Audi e-tron Concept Supercar.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
