<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span></h2>
<p>Audi has competed in various forms of <a href="/wiki/Auto_racing" title="Auto racing">motorsports</a>. Audi's tradition in motorsport began with their former company <a href="/wiki/Auto_Union" title="Auto Union">Auto Union</a> in the 1930s. In the 1990s, Audi found success in the Touring and Super Touring categories of motor racing after success in circuit racing in North America.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rallying">Rallying</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Audi_Sport_WRC_results" title="Audi Sport WRC results">Audi Sport WRC results</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg/220px-Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg/330px-Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg/440px-Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1437" data-file-height="958" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_84_Audi_Quattro_A2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Walter_R%C3%B6hrl" title="Walter Röhrl">Walter Röhrl</a> with his Quattro A2 during the 1984 <a href="/wiki/Rally_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally Portugal">Rally Portugal</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1980, Audi released the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Quattro</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">four-wheel drive</a> (4WD) <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbocharged</a> car that went on to win <a href="/wiki/Rally_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally racing">rallies</a> and races worldwide. It is considered one of the most significant rally cars of all time, because it was one of the first to take advantage of the then-recently changed rules which allowed the use of four-wheel drive in competition racing. Many critics doubted the viability of four-wheel drive racers, thinking them to be too heavy and complex, yet the Quattro was to become a successful car. Leading its first rally it went off the road, however the rally world had been served notice 4WD was the future. The Quattro went on to achieve much success in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a>. It won the <a href="/wiki/1983_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1983 World Rally Championship season">1983</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/1984_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1984 World Rally Championship season">1984</a> (<a href="/wiki/Stig_Blomqvist" title="Stig Blomqvist">Stig Blomqvist</a>) <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_Drivers%27_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Rally Championship Drivers' Champions">drivers' titles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and brought Audi the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Rally_Championship_Constructors%27_Champions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Rally Championship Constructors' Champions">manufacturers' title</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1982 World Rally Championship season">1982</a> and 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1316" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Quattro_-_2007_Rallye_Deutschland_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro_S1" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi Quattro S1">Audi Quattro S1</a> driven at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rallye_Deutschland" title="2007 Rallye Deutschland">2007 Rallye Deutschland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1984, Audi launched the short-wheelbase <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro#Sport_Quattro" title="Audi Quattro">Sport Quattro</a> which dominated rally races in <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Rally" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Rally">Sweden</a>, with Audi taking all podium places, but succumbed to problems further into WRC contention. In <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1985 World Rally Championship season">1985</a>, after another season mired in mediocre finishes, <a href="/wiki/Walter_R%C3%B6hrl" title="Walter Röhrl">Walter Röhrl</a> finished the season in his <a href="/wiki/Audi_Quattro#Sport_Quattro_S1_E2" title="Audi Quattro">Sport Quattro S1</a>, and helped place Audi second in the manufacturers' points. Audi also received rally honours in the Hong Kong to Beijing rally in that same year. <a href="/wiki/Mich%C3%A8le_Mouton" title="Michèle Mouton">Michèle Mouton</a>, the only female driver to win a round of the World Rally Championship and a driver for Audi, took the Sport Quattro S1, now simply called the "S1", and raced in the <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak_International_Hill_Climb" title="Pikes Peak International Hill Climb">Pikes Peak International Hill Climb</a>. The 1,439-metre (4,721&#160;ft) climb race pits a driver and car to drive to the summit of the 4,302-metre (14,114&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak" title="Pikes Peak">Pikes Peak</a> mountain in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, and in 1985, Michèle Mouton set a new record of 11:25.39, and being the first woman to set a Pikes Peak record. In <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Rally_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1986 World Rally Championship season">1986</a>, Audi formally left international rally racing following an accident in <a href="/wiki/Rally_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally Portugal">Portugal</a> involving driver <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joaquim_Santos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joaquim Santos (page does not exist)">Joaquim Santos</a> in his <a href="/wiki/Ford_RS200" title="Ford RS200">Ford RS200</a>. Santos swerved to avoid hitting spectators in the road, and left the track into the crowd of spectators on the side, killing three and injuring 30. <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Unser" title="Bobby Unser">Bobby Unser</a> used an Audi in that same year to claim a new record for the Pikes Peak Hill Climb at 11:09.22.</p>
<p>In 1987, Walter Röhrl claimed the title for Audi setting a new Pikes Peak International Hill Climb record of 10:47.85 in his Audi S1, which he had retired from the WRC two years earlier. The Audi S1 employed Audi's time-tested <a href="/wiki/Straight-five_engine" title="Straight-five engine">inline-five-cylinder</a> turbocharged engine, with the final version generating 441&#160;kW (600&#160;PS; 591&#160;bhp).<sup id="cite_ref-Quattro25_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quattro25-88">[88]</a></sup> The engine was mated to a six-speed gearbox and ran on Audi's famous four-wheel drive system. All of Audi's top drivers drove this car; Hannu Mikkola, Stig Blomqvist, Walter Röhrl and Michèle Mouton. This Audi S1 started the range of Audi <a href="/wiki/Audi_S_and_RS_models#S" title="Audi S and RS models">'S' cars</a>, which now represents an increased level of sports-performance equipment within the mainstream Audi model range.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_USA">In the USA</span></h3>
<p>As Audi moved away from rallying and into circuit racing, they chose to move first into America with the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Am_Series" title="Trans-Am Series">Trans-Am</a> in 1988.</p>
<p>In 1989, Audi moved to <a href="/wiki/International_Motor_Sports_Association" title="International Motor Sports Association">International Motor Sports Association</a> (IMSA) <a href="/wiki/IMSA_GT_Championship" title="IMSA GT Championship">GTO</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_80" title="Audi 80">Audi 90</a>, however as they avoided the two major endurance events (Daytona and Sebring) despite winning on a regular basis, they would lose out on the title.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring_cars">Touring cars</span></h3>
<p>In 1990, having completed their objective to market cars in North America, Audi returned to Europe, turning first to the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Tourenwagen_Meisterschaft" title="Deutsche Tourenwagen Meisterschaft">Deutsche Tourenwagen Meisterschaft</a> (DTM) series with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_V8" title="Audi V8">Audi V8</a>, and then in 1993, being unwilling to build cars for the new formula, they turned their attention to the fast-growing <a href="/wiki/Super_Touring" title="Super Touring">Super Touring</a> series, which are a series of national championships. Audi first entered in the <a href="/wiki/French_Supertouring_Championship" title="French Supertouring Championship">French Supertourisme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Superturismo_Championship" title="Italian Superturismo Championship">Italian Superturismo</a>. In the following year, Audi would switch to the German <a href="/wiki/Super_Tourenwagen_Cup" title="Super Tourenwagen Cup">Super Tourenwagen Cup</a> (known as STW), and then to <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Touring Car Championship</a> (BTCC) the year after that.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a> (FIA), having difficulty regulating the <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel_drive_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quattro (four-wheel drive system)">quattro</a> four-wheel drive system, and the impact it had on the competitors, would eventually ban all four-wheel drive cars from competing in 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-Audi_Motorsport_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Audi_Motorsport-89">[89]</a></sup> but by then, Audi switched all their works efforts to <a href="/wiki/Sports_car_racing" title="Sports car racing">sports car racing</a>.</p>
<p>By 2000, Audi would still compete in the US with their <a href="/wiki/Audi_RS4#B5" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi RS4">RS4</a> for the <a href="/wiki/SPEED_World_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="SPEED World Challenge">SCCA Speed World GT Challenge</a>, through dealer/team <a href="/wiki/Champion_Racing" title="Champion Racing">Champion Racing</a> competing against Corvettes, Vipers, and smaller BMWs (where it is one of the few series to permit 4WD cars). In 2003, Champion Racing entered an <a href="/wiki/Audi_RS6#C5" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi RS6">RS6</a>. Once again, the quattro four-wheel drive was superior, and Champion Audi won the championship. They returned in 2004 to defend their title, but a newcomer, Cadillac with the new Omega Chassis CTS-V, gave them a run for their money. After four victories in a row, the Audis were sanctioned with several negative changes that deeply affected the car's performance. Namely, added ballast weights, and Champion Audi deciding to go with different tyres, and reducing the boost pressure of the turbocharger.</p>
<p>In 2004, after years of competing with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">TT-R</a> in the revitalised DTM series, with privateer team Abt Racing/<a href="/wiki/Christian_Abt" title="Christian Abt">Christian Abt</a> taking the 2002 title with <a href="/wiki/Laurent_A%C3%AFello" title="Laurent Aïello">Laurent Aïello</a>, Audi returned as a full factory effort to touring car racing by entering two factory supported <a href="/wiki/Joest_Racing" title="Joest Racing">Joest Racing</a> <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4#Audi_Sport_A4_DTM" title="Audi A4">A4 DTM</a> cars.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="24_Hours_of_Le_Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Audi_vehicles#Le_Mans_prototypes" title="List of Audi vehicles">List of Audi vehicles §&#160;Le Mans prototypes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_R10_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_R10_1.JPG/220px-Audi_R10_1.JPG" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_R10_1.JPG/330px-Audi_R10_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Audi_R10_1.JPG/440px-Audi_R10_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2520" data-file-height="1411" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_R10_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Audi_R10_TDI" title="Audi R10 TDI">Audi R10 TDI</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi began racing prototype sportscars in 1999, debuting at the Le Mans 24 hour. Two car concepts were developed and raced in their first season - the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8R" title="Audi R8R">Audi R8R</a> (open-cockpit 'roadster' prototype) and the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R8C" title="Audi R8C">Audi R8C</a> (closed-cockpit 'coupé' GT-prototype). The R8R scored a credible podium on its racing debut at Le Mans and was the concept which Audi continued to develop into the 2000 season due to favourable rules for open-cockpit prototypes.</p>
<p>However, most of the competitors (such as BMW, Toyota, Mercedes and Nissan) retired at the end of 1999. The factory-supported <a href="/wiki/Joest_Racing" title="Joest Racing">Joest Racing</a> team won at Le Mans three times in a row with the Audi R8 (2000–2002), as well as winning every race in the <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a> in its first year. Audi also sold the car to customer teams such as <a href="/wiki/Champion_Racing" title="Champion Racing">Champion Racing</a>.</p>
<p>In 2003, two <a href="/wiki/Bentley_Speed_8" title="Bentley Speed 8">Bentley Speed 8s</a>, with engines designed by Audi, and driven by Joest drivers <i>loaned</i> to the fellow <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> company, competed in the GTP class, and finished the race in the top two positions, while the Champion Racing R8 finished third overall, and first in the LMP900 class. Audi returned to the winner's podium at the 2004 race, with the top three finishers all driving R8s: Audi Sport Japan Team Goh finished first, Audi Sport UK Veloqx second, and Champion Racing third.</p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2005_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2005 24 Hours of Le Mans">2005 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>, Champion Racing entered two R8s, along with an R8 from the Audi PlayStation Team <a href="/wiki/Oreca" title="Oreca">Oreca</a>. The R8s (which were built to old LMP900 regulations) received a narrower air inlet restrictor, reducing power, and an additional 50&#160;kg (110&#160;lb) of weight compared to the newer LMP1 chassis. On average, the R8s were about 2–3&#160;seconds off pace compared to the <a href="/wiki/Pescarolo_Sport" title="Pescarolo Sport">Pescarolo</a>–<a href="/wiki/Judd_(engine)" title="Judd (engine)">Judd</a>. But with a team of excellent drivers and experience, both Champion R8s were able to take first and third, while the Oreca team took fourth. The Champion team was also the first American team to win Le Mans since the Gulf Ford GTs in 1967. This also ends the long era of the R8; however, its replacement for 2006, called the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R10_TDI" title="Audi R10 TDI">Audi R10 TDI</a>, was unveiled on 13 December 2005.</p>
<p>The R10 <a href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">TDI</a> employed many new and innovative features, the most notable being the <a href="/wiki/Twin-turbo" title="Twin-turbo">twin-turbocharged</a> <a href="/wiki/Direct_fuel_injection" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct fuel injection">direct injection</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engine</a>. It was first raced in the <a href="/wiki/2006_12_Hours_of_Sebring" title="2006 12 Hours of Sebring">2006 12 Hours of Sebring</a> as a race-test in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2006_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2006 24 Hours of Le Mans">2006 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>, which it later went on to win. Audi has been on the forefront of sports car racing, claiming a historic win in the first diesel sports car at 12 Hours of Sebring (the car was developed with a Diesel engine due to ACO regulations that favor diesel engines). As well as winning the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> in 2006 making history, the R10 TDI has also shown its capabilities by beating the <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_908_HDi_FAP" title="Peugeot 908 HDi FAP">Peugeot 908 HDi FAP</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2007 24 Hours of Le Mans">2007</a>, and beating Peugeot again in <a href="/wiki/2008_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2008 24 Hours of Le Mans">2008</a>, (however Peugeot won the 24h in 2009) and, in a podium clean-sweep by proving its reliability throughout the race (compared to all four 908 entries retired before the end of the race) while breaking a new distance record (set way back by the <a href="/wiki/Porsche_917" title="Porsche 917">Porsche 917</a>K of <a href="/wiki/Martini_Racing" title="Martini Racing">Martini Racing</a> in <a href="/wiki/1971_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="1971 24 Hours of Le Mans">1971</a>), in <a href="/wiki/2010_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2010 24 Hours of Le Mans">2010</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R15_TDI" title="Audi R15 TDI">R15 TDI Plus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audi's sports car racing success would continue with the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R18" title="Audi R18">Audi R18</a>'s victory at the <a href="/wiki/2011_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2011 24 Hours of Le Mans">2011 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Audi_Sport_Team_Joest" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi Sport Team Joest">Audi Sport Team Joest</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beno%C3%AEt_Tr%C3%A9luyer" title="Benoît Tréluyer">Benoît Tréluyer</a> earned Audi their first <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a> in five years while the team's sister car locked out the front row.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_Audi_Front_Row_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_Audi_Front_Row-91">[91]</a></sup> Early accidents eliminated two of Audi's three entries, but the sole remaining <a href="/wiki/Audi_R18_TDI" class="mw-redirect" title="Audi R18 TDI">Audi R18 TDI</a> of Tréluyer, <a href="/wiki/Marcel_F%C3%A4ssler_(racing_driver)" title="Marcel Fässler (racing driver)">Marcel Fässler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Lotterer" title="André Lotterer">André Lotterer</a> held off the trio of <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_908" title="Peugeot 908">Peugeot 908s</a> to claim victory by a margin of 13.8 seconds.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Le_Mans_Series">American Le Mans Series</span></h3>
<p>Audi entered a factory racing team run by <a href="/wiki/Joest_Racing" title="Joest Racing">Joest Racing</a> into the American Le Mans Series under the Audi Sport North America name in 2000. This was a successful operation with the team winning on its debut in the series at the 2000 12 Hours of Sebring. Factory backed Audi R8s were the dominant car in ALMS taking 25 victories between 2000 and the end of the 2002 season. In 2003 Audi sold customer cars to <a href="/wiki/Champion_Racing" title="Champion Racing">Champion Racing</a> as well as continuing to race the factory Audi Sport North America team. Champion Racing won many races as a private team running Audi R8s and eventually replaced Team Joest as the Audi Sport North America between 2006 and 2008. Since 2009 Audi has not taken part in full American Le Mans Series Championships, but has competed in the series opening races at Sebring, using the 12-hour race as a test for Le Mans, and also as part of the <a href="/wiki/2012_FIA_World_Endurance_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 FIA World Endurance Championship season">2012 FIA World Endurance Championship season</a> calendar.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Le_Mans_Series">European Le Mans Series</span></h3>
<p>Audi participated in the <a href="/wiki/2003_1000km_of_Le_Mans" class="mw-redirect" title="2003 1000km of Le Mans">2003 1000km of Le Mans</a> which was a one-off sports car race in preparation for the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2004_European_Le_Mans_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2004 European Le Mans Series (page does not exist)">2004 European Le Mans Series</a>. The factory team Audi Sport UK won races and the championship in the 2004 season but Audi was unable to match their sweeping success of Audi Sport North America in the American Le Mans Series, partly due to the arrival of a factory competitor in LMP1, Peugeot. The French manufacturer's <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_908_HDi_FAP" title="Peugeot 908 HDi FAP">908 HDi FAP</a> became the car to beat in the series from 2008 onwards with 20 LMP wins. However, Audi were able to secure the championship in 2008 even though Peugeot scored more race victories in the season.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Endurance_Championship">World Endurance Championship</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012">2012</span></h4>
<p>In 2012, the FIA sanctioned a <a href="/wiki/FIA_World_Endurance_Championship" title="FIA World Endurance Championship">World Endurance Championship</a> which would be organised by the ACO as a continuation of the ILMC. Audi competed won the first WEC race at Sebring and followed this up with a further three successive wins, including the <a href="/wiki/2012_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2012 24 Hours of Le Mans">2012 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>. Audi scored a final 5th victory in the 2012 WEC in Bahrain and were able to win the inaugural WEC Manufacturers' Championship.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span></h4>
<p>As defending champions, Audi once again entered the <a href="/wiki/Audi_R18" title="Audi R18">Audi R18 e-tron quattro</a> chassis into the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIA_World_Endurance_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 FIA World Endurance Championship season">2013 WEC</a> and the team won the first five consecutive races, including the <a href="/wiki/2013_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2013 24 Hours of Le Mans">2013 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>. The victory at Round 5, <a href="/wiki/Circuit_of_the_Americas" title="Circuit of the Americas">Circuit of the Americas</a>, was of particular significance as it marked the 100th win for Audi in Le Mans prototypes.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Audi secured their second consecutive WEC Manufacturers' Championship at Round 6 after taking second place and half points in the red-flagged Fuji race.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span></h4>
<p>For the 2014 season Audi entered a redesigned and upgraded R18 e-tron quattro which featured a 2 <a href="/wiki/Megajoule" class="mw-redirect" title="Megajoule">MJ</a> energy recovery system. As defending champions, Audi would once again face a challenge in <a href="/wiki/LMP1" class="mw-redirect" title="LMP1">LMP1</a> from <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, and additionally from <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> who returned to endurance racing after a 16-year absence. The season opening <a href="/w/index.php?title=6hrs_of_Silverstone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="6hrs of Silverstone (page does not exist)">6hrs of Silverstone</a> was a disaster for Audi who saw both cars retire from the race, marking the first time that an Audi car has failed to score a podium in a <a href="/wiki/FIA_World_Endurance_Championship" title="FIA World Endurance Championship">World Endurance Championship</a> race.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_E">Formula E</span></h3>
<p>Audi provide factory support to <a href="/wiki/Abt_Sportsline" title="Abt Sportsline">Abt Sportsline</a> in the <a href="/wiki/FIA_Formula_E_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIA Formula E Championship">FIA Formula E Championship</a>, The team competed under the title of <b>Audi Sport Abt Formula E Team</b> in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2014-15_Formula_E_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2014-15 Formula E season">2014-15 Formula E season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> On 13 February 2014 the team announced its driver line up as <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Abt" title="Daniel Abt">Daniel Abt</a> and World Endurance Championship driver <a href="/wiki/Lucas_di_Grassi" title="Lucas di Grassi">Lucas di Grassi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_One">Formula One</span></h3>
<p>Audi has been linked to <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> in recent years but has always resisted due to the company's opinion that it is not relevant to road cars, but hybrid power unit technology has been adopted into the sport, swaying the company's view and encouraging research into the program by former <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> team principal <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Domenicali" title="Stefano Domenicali">Stefano Domenicali</a>.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png/220px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png/330px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png/440px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1040" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Audi_Sans.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The typeface Audi Sans (used 1997-2009)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png/220px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png/330px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png/440px-Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1040" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Audi_Type.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The typeface Audi Type (used since 2009)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Audi emblem is four overlapping rings that represent the four <a href="/wiki/Marque" class="mw-redirect" title="Marque">marques</a> of Auto Union. The Audi emblem symbolises the amalgamation of Audi with DKW, Horch and Wanderer: the first ring from the left represents Audi, the second represents DKW, third is Horch, and the fourth and last ring Wanderer.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The design is popularly believed to have been the idea of <a href="/wiki/Klaus_von_Oertzen" title="Klaus von Oertzen">Klaus von Oertzen</a>, the director of sales at <a href="/wiki/Wanderer_(car)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wanderer (car)">Wanderer</a> - when <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> was chosen as the host city for the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> and that a form of the Olympic logo symbolized the newly established Auto Union's desire to succeed.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Somewhat ironically, the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> later sued Audi in the International Trademark Court in 1995, where they lost.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The original "Audi" script, with the distinctive slanted tails on the "A" and "d" was created for the historic Audi company in 1920 by the famous graphic designer <a href="/wiki/Lucian_Bernhard" title="Lucian Bernhard">Lucian Bernhard</a>, and was resurrected when Volkswagen revived the brand in 1965. Following the demise of NSU in 1977, less prominence was given to the four rings, in preference to the "Audi" script encased within a black (later red) ellipse, and was commonly displayed next to the Volkswagen roundel when the two brands shared a dealer network under the <b>V.A.G</b> banner. The ellipse (known as the Audi Oval) was phased out after 1994, when Audi formed its own independent dealer network, and prominence was given back to the four rings - at the same time Audi Sans (a derivative of <a href="/wiki/Univers" title="Univers">Univers</a>) was adopted as the font for all marketing materials, corporate communications and was also used in the vehicles themselves.</p>
<p>As part of Audi's centennial celebration in 2009, the company updated the logo, changing the <a href="/wiki/Font" title="Font">font</a> to left-aligned Audi Type, and altering the shading for the overlapping rings.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The revised logo was designed by Rayan Abdullah.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audi developed a Corporate Sound concept, with Audi Sound Studio designed for producing the Corporate Sound.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The Corporate Sound project began with sound agency Klangerfinder GmbH &amp; Co KG and s12 GmbH. Audio samples were created in Klangerfinder's sound studio in Stuttgart, becoming part of Audi Sound Studio collection. Other Audi Sound Studio components include The Brand Music Pool, The Brand Voice.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Audi also developed Sound Branding Toolkit including certain instruments, sound themes, rhythm and car sounds which all are supposed to reflect the AUDI sound character.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Audi started using a beating heart sound trademark beginning in 1996. An updated heartbeat sound logo, developed by agencies KLANGERFINDER GmbH &amp; Co KG of Stuttgart and S12 GmbH of Munich, was first used in 2010 in an <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a> commercial with the slogan "The Art of Progress."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slogans">Slogans</span></h4>
<p>Audi's corporate <a href="/wiki/Tagline" title="Tagline">tagline</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/Vorsprung_durch_Technik" class="mw-redirect" title="Vorsprung durch Technik">Vorsprung durch Technik</a></i>, meaning <i>"Progress through Technology"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The German-language tagline is used in many European countries, including the United Kingdom, and in other markets, such as Latin America, Oceania and parts of Asia including Japan. A few years ago, the North American tagline was <i>"Innovation through technology"</i>, but in Canada the German tagline <i>Vorsprung durch Technik</i> was used in advertising. Since 2007, Audi has used the slogan "Truth in Engineering" in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> However, since the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_emissions_violations" class="mw-redirect" title="Volkswagen emissions violations">Audi emissions testing scandal</a> came to light in September 2015, this slogan was lambasted for being discordant with reality.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In fact, just hours after disgraced Volkswagen CEO <a href="/wiki/Martin_Winterkorn" title="Martin Winterkorn">Martin Winterkorn</a> admitted to cheating on emissions data, an advertisement during the 2015 Primetime Emmy Awards promoted Audi's latest advances in low emissions technology with Kermit the Frog stating, "It's not that easy being green."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was first used in English-language advertising after Sir John Hegarty of the <a href="/wiki/Bartle_Bogle_Hegarty" title="Bartle Bogle Hegarty">Bartle Bogle Hegarty</a> advertising agency visited the Audi factory in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-rice-oxley_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-rice-oxley-112">[112]</a></sup> In the original British television commercials, the phrase was voiced by <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Palmer_(actor)" title="Geoffrey Palmer (actor)">Geoffrey Palmer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-rice-oxley_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-rice-oxley-112">[112]</a></sup> After its repeated use in advertising campaigns, the phrase found its way into popular culture, including the British comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Only_Fools_and_Horses" title="Only Fools and Horses">Only Fools and Horses</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Zooropa_(song)" title="Zooropa (song)">Zooropa</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Blur_(Blur_album)" title="Blur (Blur album)">Blur</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Parklife_(song)" title="Parklife (song)">Parklife</a>". Similar-sounding phrases have also been used, including as the punchline for a joke in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Lock,_Stock,_and_Two_Smoking_Barrels" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock, Stock, and Two Smoking Barrels">Lock, Stock, and Two Smoking Barrels</a></i> and in the British TV series <a href="/wiki/Peep_Show_(TV_series)" title="Peep Show (TV series)">Peep Show</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Typography">Typography</span></h4>
<p>Audi Sans (based on <a href="/wiki/Univers" title="Univers">Univers</a> Extended) was originally created in 1997 by Ole Schäfer for <a href="/wiki/MetaDesign" title="MetaDesign">MetaDesign</a>. MetaDesign was later commissioned for a new corporate typeface called Audi Type, designed by Paul van der Laan and Pieter van Rosmalen of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bold_Monday&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bold Monday (page does not exist)">Bold Monday</a>. The font began to appear in Audi's 2009 products and marketing materials.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/220px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" width="220" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/330px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/440px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="1786" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi sponsors <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Audi is a strong partner of different kinds of sports. In <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, long partnerships exist between Audi and domestic clubs including <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>, <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Nuremberg" class="mw-redirect" title="1. FC Nuremberg">1. FC Nuremberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertha_BSC" title="Hertha BSC">Hertha Berlin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> and international clubs including <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelsea FC">Chelsea FC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid CF</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/AC_Milan" class="mw-redirect" title="AC Milan">AC Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajax Amsterdam">Ajax Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perspolis_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Perspolis F.C.">Perspolis F.C.</a>. Audi also sponsors winter sports: The Audi FIS Alpine Ski World Cup is named after the company. Additionally, Audi supports the <a href="/wiki/German_Ski_Association" title="German Ski Association">German Ski Association</a> (DSV) as well as the alpine skiing national teams of Switzerland, Sweden, Finland, France, Liechtenstein, Italy, Austria and the US. For almost two decades Audi fosters golf sport: for example with the Audi quattro Cup and the HypoVereinsbank Ladies German Open presented by Audi. In sailing, Audi is engaged in the Medcup regatta and supports the team <a href="/wiki/Luna_Rossa_Challenge" title="Luna Rossa Challenge">Luna Rossa</a> during the Louis Vuitton Pacific Series and also is the primary sponsor of the Melges 20 sailboat. Further, Audi sponsors the regional teams <a href="/wiki/ERC_Ingolstadt" title="ERC Ingolstadt">ERC Ingolstadt</a> (hockey) and <a href="/wiki/FC_Ingolstadt_04" title="FC Ingolstadt 04">FC Ingolstadt 04</a> (soccer).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In 2009, the year of Audi's 100th anniversary, the company organized the <a href="/wiki/Audi_Cup" title="Audi Cup">Audi Cup</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Audi also sponsor the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> as well. In October 2010 they agreed to a three sponsorship year-deal with <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Audi also sponsors the England <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">Polo</a> Team and holds the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_Polo_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Audi Polo Awards (page does not exist)">Audi Polo Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multitronic_campaign">Multitronic campaign</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Centre_Sydney,_Zetland,_New_South_Wales_(2010-07-10)_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg/220px-Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg/330px-Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg/440px-Audi_Centre_Sydney%2C_Zetland%2C_New_South_Wales_%282010-07-10%29_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi_Centre_Sydney,_Zetland,_New_South_Wales_(2010-07-10)_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audi Centre Sydney, <a href="/wiki/Zetland,_New_South_Wales" title="Zetland, New South Wales">Zetland, New South Wales</a>, Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, Audi promoted the new <a href="/wiki/Multitronic" title="Multitronic">multitronic</a> <a href="/wiki/Continuously_variable_transmission" title="Continuously variable transmission">continuously variable transmission</a> with television commercials throughout Europe, featuring an impersonator of musician and actor <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Prototypical" class="mw-redirect" title="Prototypical">prototypical</a> dashboard figure – later named "<a href="/wiki/Wackel-Elvis" title="Wackel-Elvis">Wackel-Elvis</a>" ("Wobble Elvis" or "Wobbly Elvis") – appeared in the commercials to demonstrate the smooth ride in an Audi equipped with the multitronic transmission. The dashboard figure was originally intended for use in the commercials only, but after they aired the demand for Wackel-Elvis fans grew among fans and the figure was mass-produced in China and marketed by Audi in their factory outlet store.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_TDI">Audi TDI</span></h3>
<p>As part of Audi's attempt to promote its Diesel technology in 2009, the company began Audi Mileage Marathon. The driving tour featured a fleet of 23 Audi TDI vehicles from 4 models (<a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">Audi Q7</a> 3.0 TDI, <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q5" title="Audi Q5">Audi Q5</a> 3.0 TDI, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a> 3.0 TDI, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A3" title="Audi A3">Audi A3</a> Sportback 2.0 TDI with S tronic transmission) travelling across the American continent from New York to Los Angeles, passing major cities like Chicago, Dallas and Las Vegas during the 13 daily stages, as well as natural wonders including the Rocky Mountains, Death Valley and the Grand Canyon.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>As part of 2014 model year Audi TDI vehicles launch in the US, 3 television commercials ("The Station", "Future", "Range") were produced. In the 60-second 'The Station' ad, a woman at a fueling station reaches for the diesel pump to fill up her Audi A6. In a dramatic fashion, unsuspecting onlookers race towards her and they can't imagine the luxury vehicle is in fact a diesel. The spot ends with the tagline "It's time to rethink diesel – join the club." "The Station" appeared on primetime network and cable 2013 fall programming including Agents of S.H.I.E.L.D, Modern Family, The Big Bang Theory, Hostages, Sons of Anarchy and NBC NFL Sunday Night Football. The 15-second "Range" ad demonstrates the potential to drive from New York to Chicago on a single tank of gas, covering a range of approximately 790 miles. In the 15-second "Future" ad, viewers see the potential for clean diesel as today's leading alternative fuel solution and an intelligent choice for those on the leading-edge. Audi TDI provides drivers with 30% better fuel economy and range without compromises on performance and design. In addition to the three new television spots, Audi also tried to dispel the most common myths of diesel – gas station availability, the smell and perception associated with an older generation of diesel vehicles, weak performance – in a series of four online video shorts that would roll out over the next two months on the Audi YouTube channel (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.youtube.com/audiusa">https://www.youtube.com/audiusa</a>). The spots also will appear on The Washington Post and Slate.com in a custom user-generated content hub through 2013-10-31. In addition to standard and high-impact ads, the content hub features custom videos, articles and infographics, along with relevant social conversations. The Audi TDI clean diesel campaign also features print ads that reinforce the message "the future of fuel is here now." Print ads would roll out in select automotive buff books in fall 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> 'The Station' ad was premiered in Canada in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> 'The Station' (also called 'The Moment of Truth') ad was produced by Venables Bell &amp; Partners, Biscuit Filmworks, Final Cut.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>As part of 2014 model year Audi TDI vehicles launch in the US, the 'Truth in 48' driving challenge took place from Audi Pacific dealership at Los Angeles to New York in 48 hours or less, began at 9 a.m. PDT on 2013-09-07. The Coast-to-coast attempt used 2014 Audi A6 TDI and Audi A7 TDI and a 2014 Audi Q5 TDI crossover as the support vehicle, with teams of eight noted hypermilers and four journalists.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_e-tron">Audi e-tron</span></h3>
<p>The next phase of technology Audi is developing is the <a href="/wiki/Audi_e-tron" title="Audi e-tron">e-tron</a> electric drive powertrain system. They have shown several concept cars as of March 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Audi&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, each with different levels of size and performance. The original e-tron concept shown at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_motor_show" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt motor show">Frankfurt motor show</a> is based on the platform of the R8 and has been scheduled for limited production. Power is provided by electric motors at all four wheels. The second concept was shown at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Motor_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Detroit Motor Show">Detroit Motor Show</a>. Power is provided by two electric motors at the rear axle. This concept is also considered to be the direction for a future mid-engined gas-powered 2-seat performance coupe. The <a href="/wiki/Audi_A1" title="Audi A1">Audi A1</a> e-tron concept, based on the Audi A1 production model, is a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicle</a> with a range extending <a href="/wiki/Wankel_rotary_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Wankel rotary engine">Wankel rotary engine</a> to provide power after the initial charge of the battery is depleted. It is the only concept of the three to have range extending capability. The car is powered through the front wheels, always using electric power.</p>
<p>It is all set to be displayed at the Auto Expo 2012 in New Delhi, India, from 5 January. Powered by a 1.4 litre engine, and can cover a distance up to 54&#160;km s on a single charge. The e-tron was also shown in the 2013 blockbuster film Iron Man 3 and was driven by Tony Stark (Iron Man).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_video_games">In video games</span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Home" title="PlayStation Home">PlayStation Home</a>, the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>'s online community-based service, Audi has supported Home by releasing a dedicated <a href="/wiki/List_of_PlayStation_Home_Game_Spaces#Non-gaming_Company_Spaces" title="List of PlayStation Home Game Spaces">Home space</a> in the European version of Home. Audi is the first carmaker to develop a space for Home. On 17 December 2009, Audi released the Audi Space as two spaces; the Audi Home Terminal and the Audi Vertical Run.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The Audi Home Terminal features an Audi TV channel delivering video content, an Internet Browser feature, and a view of a city. The Audi Vertical Run is where users can access the mini-game Vertical Run, a futuristic mini-game featuring Audi's e-tron concept. Players collect energy and race for the highest possible speeds and the fastest players earn a place in the Audi apartments located in a large tower in the centre of the Audi Space. In both the Home Terminal and Vertical Run spaces, there are teleports where users can teleport back and forth between the two spaces. Audi has stated that additional content will be added in 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (August 2016)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
